1e115 RSRC
1e11c LVINLBVWe
1e12e 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
1e269 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
1e3f9 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1e4b1 GPIB status vector:
1e4c6 status[0] - Device Clear State
1e4e5  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1e507  status[2] - Listener Active State
1e52b status[3] - Talker Active State
1e54c status[4] - Attention line asserted
1e571 status[5] -
1e57d Controller In Charge
1e592  status[6] - Remote State
1e5ac  status[7] - Lockout State
1e5c8 status[8] - I/O Completed 
1e5e4 status[9] - not used
1e5f9  status[10]- not used
1e60f  status[11]- not used
1e626 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1e64e status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1e66e  status[14]- Timeout occured
1e68b  status[15]- GPIB error detected
1e6af GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1e6e4 GPIB Error:
1e6f5 -No error
1e704 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
1e72b -No listeners detected on write
1e750 -Controller not addressed correctly
1e779 -Invalid argument(s)
1e794 (perhaps bad address string????)
1e7ba -Function requires GPIB to be SC
1e7e0 -I/O operation aborted
1e7fc -hardware not present
1e817 -DMA error
1e827 -DMA bus timeout
1e83d -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
1e864 progress
1e872 -function not implemented
1e891 -file system error
1e8a9 -shareable board exclusively owned
1e8d1 -GPIB bus error (commands)
1e8f1 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
1e90d -SRQ line cannot be cleared
1e92e -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
1e988 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
1ead6 GPIB status vector:
1eaeb status[0] - Device Clear State
1eb0a  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1eb2c  status[2] - Listener Active State
1eb50 status[3] - Talker Active State
1eb71 status[4] - Attention line asserted
1eb96 status[5] -
1eba2 Controller In Charge
1ebb7  status[6] - Remote State
1ebd1  status[7] - Lockout State
1ebed status[8] - I/O Completed 
1ec09 status[9] - not used
1ec1e  status[10]- not used
1ec34  status[11]- not used
1ec4b status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1ec73 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1ec93  status[14]- Timeout occured
1ecb0  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

2c93c GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set. 
2c972 GPIB Error:
2c983 -No error
2c992 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
2c9b9 -No listeners detected on write
2c9de -Controller not addressed correctly
2ca07 -Invalid argument(s)
2ca22 (perhaps bad address string????)
2ca48 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
2ca6e -I/O operation aborted
2ca8a -hardware not present
2caa5 -DMA error
2cab5 -DMA bus timeout
2cacb -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
2caf2 progress
2cb00 -function not implemented
2cb1f -file system error
2cb37 -shareable board exclusively owned
2cb5f -GPIB bus error (commands)
2cb7f -Serial Poll Byte Lost
2cb9b -SRQ line cannot be cleared
2cbbc -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
2cc18 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2ccd0 GPIB status vector:
2cce5 status[0] - Device Clear State
2cd04  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2cd26  status[2] - Listener Active State
2cd4a status[3] - Talker Active State
2cd6b status[4] - Attention line asserted
2cd90 status[5] -
2cd9c Controller In Charge
2cdb1  status[6] - Remote State
2cdcb  status[7] - Lockout State
2cde7 status[8] - I/O Completed 
2ce03 status[9] - not used
2ce18  status[10]- not used
2ce2e  status[11]- not used
2ce45 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2ce6d status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2ce8d  status[14]- Timeout occured
2ceaa  status[15]- GPIB error detected
2cecc This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
2cfc9 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
2d0ff The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
2d170   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
2d1a0  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
2d1cf  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device. 
2d24b GPIB status vector:
2d260 status[0] - Device Clear State
2d27f  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2d2a1  status[2] - Listener Active State
2d2c5 status[3] - Talker Active State
2d2e6 status[4] - Attention line asserted
2d30b status[5] -
2d317 Controller In Charge
2d32c  status[6] - Remote State
2d346  status[7] - Lockout State
2d362 status[8] - I/O Completed 
2d37e status[9] - not used
2d393  status[10]- not used
2d3a9  status[11]- not used
2d3c0 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2d3e8 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2d408  status[14]- Timeout occured
2d425  status[15]- GPIB error detected

6ade3 LVINLBVWg`
6adf5 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
6af29 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
6b03d VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
6b196 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

9ade3 (I32) 
9adea A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
9aee6 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
9b03f      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
9b073      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
9b0ad      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
9b0e6      error, and a positive value is a warning.
9b116      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
9b148      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
9b179 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

9b21c ERROR
9b223 (ABC) 
9b22a The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
9b2e1 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
9b3e3      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
9b416      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
9b445      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
9b47f      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
9b4b8      error, and a positive value is a warning.
9b4e8      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
9b517      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
9b548 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

b5aca (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
b5c23      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b5c57      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
b5c91      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
b5cca      error, and a positive value is a warning.
b5cfa      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
b5d2c      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b5d5d [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b5de9 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
b5ecf GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
b5efe VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
b5f1d GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
b5f57 Optional Parameter Default Values:
b5f7a     bd - GPIB board (0)
b5f92     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
b5fbb     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
b5fe8     logical addr - VXI logical address 
b6011 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
b6073 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

b608d ERROR
b6093 no error
b609c ERROR
b60a3 (ABC) 
b60aa The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
b6161 (I32) 
b6168 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
b6263 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
b6365      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b6398      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
b63c7      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
b6401      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
b643a      error, and a positive value is a warning.
b646a      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
b6499      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b64ca ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

d4fa6 &Opens an existing file, creates a new file, or replaces an existing file, programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern, and you can specify open and deny modes when opening a file, plus group and permission when creating a new file. Use this VI with the intermediate Write File+ or Read File+ VIs described below.
d5144 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
d5220 function is the operation to perform:
d5248 0 (open) opens an existing file.  Error 7 occurs if the file cannot be found.
d5299 1 (open or create) opens an existing file or creates a new file if one does not exist.
d52f2 2 (create or replace) creates a new file or replaces a file if it exists and you give permission.  Replacement is done by opening the file and setting EOF to 0.  Error 43 occurs if the user elects to disallow the replacement using dialog.  
d53e5 3 (create) creates a new file.  Error 8 occurs if the file already exists.
d5431 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if function=0 and the file does not exist, or if function=2 or 3 and the file exists.
d54c2 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
d5522 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
d557f start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
d5635 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
d56df error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
d58f5 new file path is the path of the file opened or created.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open or create using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
d59e0 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
d5a4b file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
d5aa4 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

e62e1 lprompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories (or folders) in the file dialog.
e6382 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory (or folder) in a file dialog. The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory (or folder) shown in a file dialog.
e6466 \default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
e6541 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories (or folders). See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
e6603 =!L#X
e6622 new file path is the path of the file opened or created. You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open or create using dialog. new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
e670e Astatus is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.
e67dd *error in is a cluster of three elements (status, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existence of any error proceeding the execution of the VI. The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.
e690c vsource is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
e6994 0code is the error code; the default value is 0.
e6a28 c<'[
e6a43 file path is the path name of the file. If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file. Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.
e6b1a irefnum is the reference number of the open file. The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
e6b88 %status is TRUE if an error occurred.
e6bc5 function is the operation to perform:
e6bef opens an existing file. Error 7 occurs if the file cannot be found.
e6c37 opens an existing file or creates a new file if one does not exist.
e6c7f creates a new file or replaces a file if it exists and you give permission. Replacement is done by opening the file and setting EOF to 0. Error 43 occurs if the user elects to disallow the replacement using dialog. 
e6d5b creates a new file. Error 8 occurs if the file already exists.
e6dce code is the error code.
e6dea Psource is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
e6e41 )error out is a cluster of three elements (status, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI. If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
e6fad Xfile size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
e700b advisory dialog? Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if function=0 and the file does not exist, or if function=2 or 3 and the file exists.

f0621 Open/Create/Replace File.vi
f1b67 *Writes a string of characters to a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the end of file.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not write if an incoming error occurs.
f1c46 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
f1c78 pos mode specifies where the write begins relative to pos offset:
f1cbf at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
f1cf2 at the end of the file plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
f1d3b at the current file mark plus pos offset.
f1d66 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
f1dee character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
f1e27 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert the LabVIEW end of line marker to the platform-specific marker.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
f1eb3 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
f20c9 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
f210f mark after write is the location of the character following the last character written.
f2168 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

f3b4b GOpens an existing file programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern.   Error 7 occurs if the file does not exist.  Use this VI with the intermediate level Read File+ VIs described below.
f3c69 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
f3d45 advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if the file does not exist.
f3d9c prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
f3dfc default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
f3e59 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
f3f0f pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
f3fb9 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
f41cf new file path is the path of the file opened.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
f42a5 refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
f4310 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
f4369 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
f449c This subVI tests the error status output of one or more low-level functions or subVIs that output a numeric error code, and creates an error out cluster that can be wired to the Simple or General Error Handler in order to identify the error and describe it to the user.
f45ab The error in cluster is tested first.  If error? is no-error, the elements of the error codes array are tested next for non-zero values.  The first error found terminates the test, and error out identifies that error.  Use a Build Array function to assemble the individual error codes.
f46ca You can optionally use the source messages string to pass on the source of the error. Enter one line of text for each element of the error codes array.  
f4765 The error? status  is TRUE on any error.
f4797 QCloses the file on command or when in incoming error occurs and returns the file size at closure.
f47fb refnum is the reference number of the open file.
f482d close when?  Set TRUE (default) when you want to close the file when this VI is called.  Set to FALSE when you want to close the file only if this VI encounters an incoming error.  This input is useful when you use this VI inside a loop and want to close the file only on the last loop iteration or on an upstream error.  In that case, set close when? TRUE on the last iteration, and terminate the loop on the last iteration or when this VI returns an error. 
f49fa file size is the size of the file in bytes at the time the file is closed; the value is zero otherwise.
f4a63 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
f4c79 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
f4cbf error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
f4df4 Reads a string of characters from a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the current mark.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not read if an incoming error occurs.
f4ed3 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
f4f05 pos mode specifies where the reads begins relative to pos offset:
f4f4c at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
f4f7f at the end of the file plus pos offset.
f4fac at the current file mark plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
f4ff3 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
f507b count is the number of bytes to read.
f50a2 line mode  Set TRUE to read until a line marker or end of line is encounter or count characters are read.  Set FALSE (default value) to read until count characters are read or end of line is encountered.  A line mark is a carriage return, a line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed.
f51cd convert eol  Set TRUE to convert each platform-specific end of line marker to the LabVIEW marker, line feed.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
f5265 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
f547b dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
f54c1 character string is the data read from the file.
f54f3 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
f557f error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.
f56b3 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
f58f0 Writes a character string to a new byte stream file or appends the string to an existing file.  The VI opens or creates the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.

f5a73 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
f5aac append to file?  Set to TRUE if you want to append the data to a existing file; you can also set it TRUE to write to a new file.  Set to FALSE (default value) if you want to write the data to a new file or to replace an existing file.

f6656 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
f6732 number of lines is the maximum number of lines the VI reads.  The default value is -1 line, which means to read the entire file.  For this VI, a line is a character string ending with a carriage return, line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed; a string ending at the EOF; or a string that has the maximum line length specified by the max characters per line input.
f68b0 start of read offset is the position in the file, measured in characters (or bytes), at which the VI begins reading.
f6926 max characters per line is the maximum number of characters the VI reads before ending the search for the end of a line.  The default is 0, which means that there is no limit to the number of characters the VI reads.
f6a00 new file path is the path of the file from which the VI read data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
f6aeb line string is the data read from the file.
f6b18 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
f6ba4 EOF? is TRUE if you attempt to read past the end of file.

ff1e5 compatWriteText.vi
ff243 *Writes a string of characters to a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the end of file.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not write if an incoming error occurs.
ff322 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
ff354 pos mode specifies where the write begins relative to pos offset:
ff39b at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
ff3ce at the end of the file plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
ff417 at the current file mark plus pos offset.
ff442 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
ff4ca character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
ff503 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert the LabVIEW end of line marker to the platform-specific marker.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
ff58f error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
ff7a5 dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
ff7eb mark after write is the location of the character following the last character written.
ff844 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

19f4b3 GOpens an existing file programmatically or interactively using dialog.  You can optionally specify a dialog prompt, default file name, start path, or filter pattern.   Error 7 occurs if the file does not exist.  Use this VI with the intermediate level Read File+ VIs described below.
19f5d1 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
19f6ad advisory dialog?  Set TRUE (default) if you want a dialog if the file does not exist.
19f704 prompt is the message that appears below the list of files and directories in the file dialog.
19f764 default name is the initial file name that appears in the selection box of the file dialog.
19f7c1 start path is the path name to the initially displayed directory in a file dialog.  The default value is Not A Path, which is the path to the last directory shown in a file dialog.
19f877 pattern is the match pattern specification to display only certain types of files or directories.  See the description of the File Dialog function for more information.
19f921 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
19fb37 new file path is the path of the file opened.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
19fc0d refnum is the reference number of the open file.  The value is Not A Refnum if the file cannot be opened.
19fc78 file size is the size of the file in bytes; it is also the location of the end of file.
19fcd1 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1a3b3c This subVI tests the error status output of one or more low-level functions or subVIs that output a numeric error code, and creates an error out cluster that can be wired to the Simple or General Error Handler in order to identify the error and describe it to the user.
1a3c4b The error in cluster is tested first.  If error? is no-error, the elements of the error codes array are tested next for non-zero values.  The first error found terminates the test, and error out identifies that error.  Use a Build Array function to assemble the individual error codes.
1a3d6a You can optionally use the source messages string to pass on the source of the error. Enter one line of text for each element of the error codes array.  
1a3e05 The error? status  is TRUE on any error.

1a6721 Find First Error.vi
1a677b QCloses the file on command or when in incoming error occurs and returns the file size at closure.
1a67df refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1a6811 close when?  Set TRUE (default) when you want to close the file when this VI is called.  Set to FALSE when you want to close the file only if this VI encounters an incoming error.  This input is useful when you use this VI inside a loop and want to close the file only on the last loop iteration or on an upstream error.  In that case, set close when? TRUE on the last iteration, and terminate the loop on the last iteration or when this VI returns an error. 
1a69de file size is the size of the file in bytes at the time the file is closed; the value is zero otherwise.
1a6a47 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1a6c5d dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1a6ca3 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1a98d5 compatReadText.vi
1a9938 Reads a string of characters from a byte stream file at the specified location; the default location is at the current mark.  The VI does incoming and internal error checking and does not read if an incoming error occurs.
1a9a17 refnum is the reference number of the open file.
1a9a49 pos mode specifies where the reads begins relative to pos offset:
1a9a90 at the beginning of the file plus pos offset.
1a9ac3 at the end of the file plus pos offset.
1a9af0 at the current file mark plus pos offset.  This is the default value.
1a9b37 pos offset specifies in characters how far from the location specified by pos mode that the operation begins.  The default value is 0.
1a9bbf count is the number of bytes to read.
1a9be6 line mode  Set TRUE to read until a line marker or end of line is encounter or count characters are read.  Set FALSE (default value) to read until count characters are read or end of line is encountered.  A line mark is a carriage return, a line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed.
1a9d11 convert eol  Set TRUE to convert each platform-specific end of line marker to the LabVIEW marker, line feed.  Set FALSE (default value) to do nothing.
1a9da9 error in is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the upstream error state, that is, the existance of any error preceeding the execution of the VI.  The VI executes normally only if no incoming error exists; otherwise it merely passes the error in value to error out.  error? is TRUE if an error occurred; the default value is FALSE.  code is the error code; the default value is 0.  source is in most cases the name of the VI or function that produced the error; the default value is an empty string.
1a9fbf dup refnum is a flow-though parameter with the same value as refnum.
1aa005 character string is the data read from the file.
1aa037 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1aa0c3 error out is a cluster of three elements (error?, code, and source) that describe the error state following the execution of the VI.  If an incoming error does not exist, the VI executes normally and error out describes the VI's error state; if an incoming error exists, error out equals error in.

1b2027 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

1b6d59 Close File+.vi
1b6db0 Writes a character string to a new byte stream file or appends the string to an existing file.  The VI opens or creates the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1b6e57 file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1b6f33 character string is the data the VI writes to the file.
1b6f6c append to file?  Set to TRUE if you want to append the data to a existing file; you can also set it TRUE to write to a new file.  Set to FALSE (default value) if you want to write the data to a new file or to replace an existing file.
1b7058 new file path is the path of the file to which the VI wrote data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.

1d4caf l7jac
1d4d6d Close File+.vi
1d4dcb *Reads a specified number of lines from a byte stream file beginning at a specified character offset.  The VI opens the file beforehand and closes it afterwards.
1d4e6e file path is the path name of the file.  If file path is empty (default value) or is Not A Path, the VI displays a File dialog box from which you can select a file.  Error 43 occurs if the user cancels the dialog.     
1d4f4a number of lines is the maximum number of lines the VI reads.  The default value is -1 line, which means to read the entire file.  For this VI, a line is a character string ending with a carriage return, line feed, or a carriage return followed by a line feed; a string ending at the EOF; or a string that has the maximum line length specified by the max characters per line input.
1d50c8 start of read offset is the position in the file, measured in characters (or bytes), at which the VI begins reading.
1d513e max characters per line is the maximum number of characters the VI reads before ending the search for the end of a line.  The default is 0, which means that there is no limit to the number of characters the VI reads.
1d5218 new file path is the path of the file from which the VI read data.  You can use this output to determine the path of a file that you open using dialog.  new file path returns Not A Path if the user selects Cancel from the dialog box.
1d5303 line string is the data read from the file.
1d5330 mark after read is the location of the file mark after the read; it points to the character in the file following the last character read.
1d53bc EOF? is TRUE if you attempt to read past the end of file.
